</div>\r\n    \r\n    <div class="divGraphAttribute">\r\n        <div class="divGraphAttributeLabel" id="descriptionLabel">\r\n            Description:\r\n        </div>\r\n        <div class="divGraphAttributeValue" id="descriptionValue">\r\n            <div id=\'tabs\'><div id=\'sticker\'><ul class=\'social\'><li id=\'mobile-item\' style=\'display:none\'><a>&#9776; MENU</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Details about the source, query and time of the data collection.\'><a href=\'#headerDescription\'>Description</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'A logo and a link for the creator of this report.\'><a href=\'#headerBrand\'>Author Description</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Summary statistics on the size and level of connectivity of the network.\'><a href=\'#headerOverallMetrics\'>Overall Metrics</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Top users ranked by a network score calculated based on the person\xe2\x80\x99s connection to otherwise disconnected groups of people.  "Betweenness" is the "Bridge Score" that measures how much a person is the only way to connect from one part of the network to another.  It is a sociological proxy for "influence".  It is different from other "social media reputation" scores in that it is local and bounded: It finds the people other people find valuable within a particular topic during a particular time.  This is in contrast to "global" reputation scores that claim to capture the value of a person in all possible contexts with a single value.  In contrast, local and bounded reputation is timely and specific to a selected topic or issue.  This score does NOT use follower count, tweet count, or retweet count as an input.  It is based on the behavior of other people towards a user to determine their value.\'><a href=\'#headerTopVertices\'>Top Influencers</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Top URLs mentioned in the data ranked by frequency along with the raw count.  This highlights relevant web resources, and when the top URLs in each of the groups are compared, this reveals the differences between segments of the network based on different patterns of URLs mentioned.  The report provides a breakout for each of the top ten groups.  These patterns are a fingerprint of what this group cares about.\'><a href=\'#headerTopURLs\'>Top URLs</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Top domains extracted from the top URLs, reveal the web sites (rather than specific pages) that are most frequently mentioned.  This can be used for to identify the websites where organic or paid content might best be placed. \'><a href=\'#headerTopDomains\'>Top Domains</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Top hashtags that co-occur with this search term ranked by frequency of mention reported along with the raw count of mentions.\'><a href=\'#headerTopHashtags\'>Top Hashtags</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Ranked and sentiment analyzed list of words that appear in the Tweets in this dataset (after a list of "stop" or "skip" words is removed).  NodeXL has a sentiment feature that categorizes words into three lists (which can be configured by the user). By default we report "Positive", "Negative", and "Angry" words.\'><a href=\'#headerTopWords\'>Top Words</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Ranked list of pairs of words that appear next to one another with the greatest frequency (after a list of "stop" or "skip" words is removed) reported along with the raw count of their appearance.\'><a href=\'#headerTopWordPairs\'>Top Word Pairs</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Top users ranked by how often their usernames appeared in the first part of a collected set of tweets (excluding the times their username appeared elsewhere in a message, which is classified as a mention instead).\'><a href=\'#headerTopRepliedTo\'>Top Replied-To</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Top users ranked by how often their usernames appeared in the collected set of tweets (excluding the times their username started a message, which is classified as a reply instead).\'><a href=\'#headerTopMentioned\'>Top Mentioned</a></li><li class=\'item\' title=\'Top users ranked by how many times they have ever tweeted as reported in their profile.  Often these are spam or low value accounts, they are inlcuded here to contrast with the set of users identified in the Top Influencers report.\'><a href=\'#headerTopTweeters\'>Top Tweeters</a></li></ul><br/></div><div id=\'headerDescription\' title=\'Details about the source, query and time of the data collection.\' class=\'ui-accordion-header ui-state-default ui-accordion-icons ui-corner-all\' style=\'cursor: pointer\'><span class=\'ui-icon ui-icon-triangle-1-s\' style=\'display:inline-block;\'></span>Description</div> <div>The graph represents a network of 9,107 Twitter users whose tweets in the requested range contained "Coronavirus", or who were replied to or mentioned in those tweets.  The network was obtained from the NodeXL Graph Server on Wednesday, 07 October 2020 at 10:43 UTC.<br/><br/>The requested start date was Tuesday, 06 October 2020 at 00:01 UTC and the maximum number of days (going backward) was 14.<br/><br/>The maximum number of tweets collected was 7,500.<br/><br/>The tweets in the network were tweeted over the 2-day, 0-hour, 1-minute period from Saturday, 03 October 2020 at 03:24 UTC to Monday, 05 October 2020 at 03:25 UTC.<br/><br/>Additional tweets that were mentioned in this data set were also collected from prior time periods.  These tweets may expand the complete time period of the data.<br/><br/>There is an edge for each "replies-to" relationship in a tweet, an edge for each "mentions" relationship in a tweet, and a self-loop edge for each tweet that is not a "replies-to" or "mentions".<br/><br/>The graph is directed.<br/><br/>The graph\'s vertices were grouped by cluster using the Clauset-Newman-Moore cluster algorithm.<br/><br/>The graph was laid out using the Harel-Koren Fast Multiscale layout algorithm.<br/><br/></div><br/><div id=\'headerBrand\' title=\'A logo and a link for the creator of this report.\' class=\'ui-accordion-header ui-state-default ui-accordion-icons ui-corner-all\' style=\'cursor: pointer\'><span class=\'ui-icon ui-icon-triangle-1-s\' style=\'display:inline-block;\'></span>Author Description</div> <div><br/><a href=\'http://connectedaction.net\'><img src=\'../Images/Image.ashx?graphID=237287&type=b\'></a><br/></div><div title=\'Density is the measure of the number edges among a group of vertices over the total possible number if everyone was connected to everyone.<br/><br/>A high graph density means that most people are connected to many others. A low graph density means that most people are not connected to many others.\'>Graph Density : 0.000111023562969582</span><br/><span id=\'overall-metrics\' title=\'Modularity is a measure of the fitness of the groups that are created in a clustered network.<br/><br/>A group is a set of vertices.<br/>Many group cluster algorithms are intended to find sets of vertices that are strongly connected and relatively separate from other strongly connected groups.<br/><br/>Modularity is the measure of the number of edges that leave a group to connect to vertices in a different group.<br/>If modularity is high, the clusters or groups created may be of low quality.  If modularity is low, the groups are well defined.\'>Modularity : 0.515795</span><br/><span id=\'overall-metrics\' title=\'NodeXL updates frequently and the current version number is provided to enable troubleshooting and to ensure older datasets are properly understood.\'>NodeXL Version : 1.0.1.441</span><br/><span id=\'overall-metrics\' title=\'Time period of the data imported from the data source.\'>Data Import : The graph represents a network of 9,107 Twitter users whose tweets in the requested range contained "Coronavirus", or who were replied to or mentioned in those tweets.
